href="https://www.airbus.com">www<wbr />.airbus<wbr />.com</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Airbus SE</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\xcb\x88</span><span title="/\xc9\x9b\xc9\x99r/: &#39;are&#39; in &#39;bare&#39;">\xc9\x9b\xc9\x99r</span><span title="&#39;b&#39; in &#39;buy&#39;">b</span><span title="/\xca\x8c/: &#39;u&#39; in &#39;cut&#39;">\xca\x8c</span><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <small>French:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/French" title="Help:IPA/French">[\xc9\x9b\xca\x81bys]</a></span>&#32;<span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:Airbus2.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c1/Airbus2.ogg" class="internal" title="Airbus2.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span>; <small>German:&#32;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Standard_German" title="Help:IPA/Standard German">[\xcb\x88\xc9\x9b\xcb\x90\xc9\x90\xcc\xafb\xca\x8as]</a></span>&#32;<span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:Airbus3.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/07/Airbus3.ogg" class="internal" title="Airbus3.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span>; <small>Spanish:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">[\xcb\x88ej\xc9\xbebus]</a></span>) is a European<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>  <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">multinational</a> <a href="/wiki/Aerospace" title="Aerospace">aerospace</a> corporation. As of 2019, Airbus is the world\'s largest airliner manufacturer and took the most airliner orders, surpassing rival <a href="/wiki/Boeing" title="Boeing">Boeing</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> It designs, manufactures and sells civil and military <a href="/wiki/Aerospace_manufacturer" title="Aerospace manufacturer">aerospace</a> products worldwide and manufactures aircraft in the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> and various other countries. The company has three divisions: <i>Commercial Aircraft (Airbus S.A.S.)</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Airbus_Defence_and_Space" title="Airbus Defence and Space">Defence and Space</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Airbus_Helicopters" title="Airbus Helicopters">Helicopters</a></i>, the third being the largest in its industry in terms of revenues and turbine helicopter deliveries.<sup id="cite_ref-About_Airbus_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-About_Airbus-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The company\'s main civil aeroplane business is conducted through the French company Airbus S.A.S.,<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> based in <a href="/wiki/Blagnac" title="Blagnac">Blagnac</a>, a suburb of <a href="/wiki/Toulouse" title="Toulouse">Toulouse</a>, with production and manufacturing facilities mostly in Europe (France, Germany, Spain, United Kingdom) but also in China, the United States and Canada. Final assembly production is based in <a href="/wiki/Toulouse" title="Toulouse">Toulouse</a>, France; <a href="/wiki/Hamburg" title="Hamburg">Hamburg</a>, Germany; <a href="/wiki/Seville" title="Seville">Seville</a>, Spain; <a href="/wiki/Tianjin" title="Tianjin">Tianjin</a>, China; <a href="/wiki/Mobile,_Alabama" title="Mobile, Alabama">Mobile</a>, United States; and <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">Montreal</a>, Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The company produces and markets the first commercially viable <a href="/wiki/Fly-by-wire#Digital_systems" title="Fly-by-wire">digital fly-by-wire</a> airliner, the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A320_family" title="Airbus A320 family">Airbus A320</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-airbuscorphis_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-airbuscorphis-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> and the world\'s largest passenger airliner, the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A380" title="Airbus A380">A380</a>. The 12,000th aircraft, an <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A220" title="Airbus A220">A220</a>, was delivered to <a href="/wiki/Delta_Air_Lines" title="Delta Air Lines">Delta Air Lines</a> on 20 May 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-Airbus20may2019_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Airbus20may2019-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> By October 2016, the global Airbus fleet have performed more than 110 million flights, totalling over 215 billion kilometres and carrying 12 billion passengers.<sup id="cite_ref-Airbus14oct2016_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Airbus14oct2016-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Airbus\'s registered headquarters is in <a href="/wiki/Leiden" title="Leiden">Leiden</a>, Netherlands, but its head office is located in Toulouse, France.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> The \'SE\' in its corporate name means it is a <i lang="la" title="Latin-language text"><a href="/wiki/Societas_Europaea" title="Societas Europaea">societas Europaea</a></i>, which enables it to be registered as European rather than Dutch. Its shares are traded in France, Germany and Spain. The company is led by CEO <a href="/wiki/Guillaume_Faury" title="Guillaume Faury">Guillaume Faury</a> and is a component of the <a href="/wiki/Euro_Stoxx_50" class="mw-redirect" title="Euro Stoxx 50">Euro Stoxx 50</a> <a href="/wiki/Stock_market_index" title="Stock market index">stock market index</a>.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toclevel-1 tocsection-32"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Airbus" title="History of Airbus">History of Airbus</a></div>\n<p>The current company is the product of consolidation in the European aerospace industry tracing back to the formation of the <i>Airbus Industrie <a href="/wiki/GIE" class="mw-redirect" title="GIE">GIE</a></i> consortium in 1970. In 2000, the European Aeronautic Defence and Space Company (EADS) <a href="/wiki/Naamloze_vennootschap" title="Naamloze vennootschap">NV</a> was established. In addition to other subsidiaries pertaining to security and space activities, EADS owned 100% of the pre-existing <a href="/wiki/Airbus_Helicopters" title="Airbus Helicopters">Eurocopter SA</a>, established in 1992, as well as 80% of Airbus Industrie GIE. In 2001, Airbus Industrie GIE was reorganised as Airbus <a href="/wiki/Soci%C3%A9t%C3%A9_par_actions_simplifi%C3%A9e" title="Soci\xc3\xa9t\xc3\xa9 par actions simplifi\xc3\xa9e">SAS</a>, a simplified <a href="/wiki/Joint-stock_company" title="Joint-stock company">joint-stock company</a>. In 2006, EADS acquired <a href="/wiki/BAE_Systems" title="BAE Systems">BAE Systems</a>\'s remaining 20% of Airbus.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> EADS NV was renamed Airbus Group NV and SE in 2014, and 2015, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-ft20140102_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ft20140102-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Airbus_Group_SE_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Airbus_Group_SE-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Due to the dominance of the Airbus SAS division within Airbus Group SE, the executive committees of the parent and subsidiary companies were aligned in January 2017, but the companies were kept as separate legal entities. The holding company was given its present name in April 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-Airbus_SE_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Airbus_SE-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r984819063">.mw-parser-output table.clade{border-spacing:0;margin:0;font-size:100%;line-height:100%;border-collapse:separate;width:auto}.mw-parser-output span.linkB{background-color:green}</style>\n</p>\n<table class="clade" style="font-size:90%;line-height:110%">\n\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<td class="clade-label first" style="border-left:none;border-right:none;border-bottom:0px solid;"><div style="display:inline;" class="nowrap"><span style="font-size:100%;"><b>Airbus SE</b></span><br /><small>(Est. 2000, renamed 2017)</small></div>\n</td>\n<td rowspan="2" class="clade-leaf">\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r984819063"/>\n<table class="clade">\n\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<td class="clade-label first"><a href="/wiki/A%C3%A9rospatiale-Matra" class="mw-redirect" title="A\xc3\xa9rospatiale-Matra">A\xc3\xa9rospatiale-Matra</a><br /><small>(Est.&#160;1999)</small>\n</td>\n<td rowspan="2" class="clade-leaf">\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r984819063"/>\n<table class="clade">\n\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<td class="clade-label 1970)</small>\n</p>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td class="clade-slabel">&#8239;\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td class="clade-label">&#8239;\n</td>\n<td rowspan="2" class="clade-leaf">\n<p><a href="/wiki/Matra" rowspan="2" class="clade-leaf">\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r984819063"/>\n<table class="clade">\n\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<td class="clade-label 1934)</small>\n</p>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td class="clade-slabel">&#8239;\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td class="clade-label">&#8239;\n</td>\n<td rowspan="2" class="clade-leaf">\n<p><a 1923)</small>\n</p>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td class="clade-slabel last">&#8239;\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td class="clade-slabel last" .navbar{float:left;text-align:left;margin-right:0.5em}</style><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Predecessors_of_Airbus_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Template:Predecessors of Airbus Group"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Template_talk:Predecessors_of_Airbus_Group&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Template talk:Predecessors of Airbus Group (page does not exist)"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Predecessors_of_Airbus_Group&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div>\n<p>The logos of Airbus Industrie GIE and Airbus SAS displayed a stylised turbine symbol, redolent of a <a href="/wiki/Jet_engine" title="Jet engine">jet engine</a>, and a font similar to <a href="/wiki/Helvetica#Variants" title="Helvetica">Helvetica Black</a>. The logo colours were reflected in the standard Airbus <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_livery" title="Aircraft livery">aircraft livery</a> in each period. The EADS logo between 2000 and 2010 combined the logos of the merged companies, <a href="/wiki/DASA" title="DASA">DaimlerChrysler Aerospace AG</a> (a four-ray star) and A\xc3\xa9rospatiale-Matra (a curved arrow), after which these elements were removed and a new font with 3D shading was chosen. This font was retained in the logos of Airbus Group NV (2014\xe2\x80\x932015) and Airbus Group SE (2015\xe2\x80\x932017), then Airbus SE:\n</p>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 185px"><div style="width: 185px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 180px;"><div style="margin:15px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:First_Airbus_logo.svg" class="gallerytext">\n<p>Original, for <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A300" title="Airbus A300">Airbus A300</a>\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 185px"><div style="width: 185px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 180px;"><div style="margin:62.5px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Airbus-group-logo.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" class="gallerytext">\n<p>2014\xe2\x80\x932017\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 185px"><div style="width: 185px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 180px;"><div style="margin:76px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Airbus_Logo_2017.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Airbus_Logo_2017.svg/150px-Airbus_Logo_2017.svg.png" decoding="async" width="150" height="28" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Airbus_Logo_2017.svg/225px-Airbus_Logo_2017.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Airbus_Logo_2017.svg/300px-Airbus_Logo_2017.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="399" data-file-height="74" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p>2017\xe2\x80\x93Present\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n</ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Products">Products</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Products">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Civilian">Civilian</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Civilian">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:A_380_meeting.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/A_380_meeting.jpg/220px-A_380_meeting.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/A_380_meeting.jpg/330px-A_380_meeting.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/A_380_meeting.jpg/440px-A_380_meeting.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1450" data-file-height="959" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:A_380_meeting.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A380" title="Airbus A380">Airbus A380</a>, the world\'s largest airliner</div></div></div>\n<p>The Airbus product line started with the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A300" title="Airbus A300">A300</a> in 1972, the world\'s first <a href="/wiki/Twin-aisle" class="mw-redirect" title="Twin-aisle">twin-aisle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Twin-engine" class="mw-redirect" title="Twin-engine">twin-engined</a> aircraft. A shorter, re-winged, re-engined variant of the A300 is known as the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A310" title="Airbus A310">A310</a>.\n</p><p>Building on its success, Airbus launched the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A320_family" title="Airbus A320 family">A320</a>, the first commercial jet to use a digital <a href="/wiki/Fly-by-wire" title="Fly-by-wire">fly-by-wire</a> control system. The A320 has been, and continues to be, a major commercial success. The <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A318" title="Airbus A318">A318</a> and <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A319" title="Airbus A319">A319</a> are shorter derivatives with some of the latter under construction for the corporate <a href="/wiki/Business_jet" title="Business jet">business jet</a> market as <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A319CJ" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A319CJ">Airbus Corporate Jets</a>. A stretched version is known as the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A321" title="Airbus A321">A321</a>. The A320 family\'s primary competitor is the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737" title="Boeing 737">Boeing 737</a> family.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The longer-range <a href="/wiki/Wide-body_aircraft" title="Wide-body aircraft">widebody</a> products\xe2\x80\x94 the twin-jet <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A330" title="Airbus A330">A330</a> and the four-engine <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A340" title="Airbus A340">A340</a>\xe2\x80\x94 have efficient wings, enhanced by <a href="/wiki/Wingtip_device" title="Wingtip device">winglets</a>. The Airbus A340-500 has an operating range of 16,700 kilometres (9,000&#160;nmi), the second longest range of any commercial jet after the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_777-200LR" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 777-200LR">Boeing 777-200LR</a> (range of 17,446&#160;km or 9,420 nautical miles).<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>All Airbus aircraft developed since then have cockpit systems similar to the A320, making it easier to train crew. Production of the four-engine A340 was ended in 2011 due to lack of sales compared to its twin-engine counterparts, such as the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_777" title="Boeing 777">Boeing 777</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-A340-ceases-production_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A340-ceases-production-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Airbus is studying a replacement for the A320 series, tentatively dubbed <a href="/wiki/Airbus_NSR" title="Airbus NSR">NSR</a>, for "New Short-Range aircraft".<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-fi_737rs_nsr_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fi_737rs_nsr-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Those studies indicated a maximum fuel efficiency gain of 9\xe2\x80\x9310% for the NSR. Airbus however opted to enhance the existing A320 design using new winglets and working on aerodynamical improvements.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> This "A320 Enhanced" should have a fuel efficiency improvement of around 4\xe2\x80\x935%, shifting the launch of an A320 replacement to 2017\xe2\x80\x932018.\n</p><p>On 24 September 2009, the COO Fabrice Bregier stated to <i><a href="/wiki/Le_Figaro" title="Le Figaro">Le Figaro</a></i> that the company would need from \xe2\x82\xac800&#160;million to \xe2\x82\xac1&#160;billion over six years to develop the new aircraft generation and preserve the company technological lead from new competitors like the Chinese Comac <a href="/wiki/COMAC_C919" class="mw-redirect" title="COMAC C919">C919</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> scheduled to operate by 2015\xe2\x80\x932020.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In July 2007, Airbus delivered its last A300 to FedEx, marking the end of the A300/A310 production line. Airbus intends to relocate Toulouse A320 final assembly activity to Hamburg, and A350/A380 production in the opposite direction as part of its Power8 organisation plan begun under ex-CEO <a href="/wiki/Christian_Streiff" title="Christian Streiff">Christian Streiff</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-forbes_20070115_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forbes_20070115-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Airbus supplied replacement parts and service for <a href="/wiki/Concorde" title="Concorde">Concorde</a> until its retirement in 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Airbus_A330-203_Qatar_Airways.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Airbus_A330-203_Qatar_Airways.jpg/220px-Airbus_A330-203_Qatar_Airways.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Airbus_A330-203_Qatar_Airways.jpg/330px-Airbus_A330-203_Qatar_Airways.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Airbus_A330-203_Qatar_Airways.jpg/440px-Airbus_A330-203_Qatar_Airways.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1650" data-file-height="1095" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Airbus_A330-203_Qatar_Airways.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>VIP aircraft <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A330" title="Airbus A330">Airbus A330</a> of <a href="/wiki/Qatar_Amiri_Flight" title="Qatar Amiri Flight">Qatar Amiri Flight</a> taxiing on Zagreb airport</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Airbus_Corporate_Jets" title="Airbus Corporate Jets">Airbus Corporate Jets</a> markets and modifies new aircraft for private and corporate customers. It has a model range that parallels the commercial aircraft offered by the company, ranging from the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A318" title="Airbus A318">A318</a> Elite to the double-deck <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A380" title="Airbus A380">Airbus A380</a> Prestige. Following the entry of the 737 based <a href="/wiki/Boeing_Business_Jet" title="Boeing Business Jet">Boeing Business Jet</a>, Airbus joined the business jet market with the A319 Corporate Jet in 1997. Although the term Airbus Corporate jet was initially used only for the A319CJ, it is now often used for all models, including the VIP widebodies. As of December 2008, 121 corporate and private jets are operating, 164 aircraft have been ordered, including an A380 Prestige and 107 A320 family Corporate Jet.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In September 2014, <a href="/wiki/Aerion" title="Aerion">Aerion</a> partnered with Airbus (mainly <a href="/wiki/Airbus_Defence_and_Space" title="Airbus Defence and Space">Airbus Defence</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> to collaborate on designing the <a href="/wiki/Aerion_AS2" title="Aerion AS2">Aerion AS2</a>, a supersonic 11-seater private business jet, hoping for a market entry in 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-wag_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wag-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> Airbus was replaced with Lockheed Martin in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><span class="anchor" id="Bag2Go"></span>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Consumer_products">Consumer products</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Consumer products">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In June 2013, Airbus announced that it was developing a range of "smart <a href="/wiki/Suitcase" title="Suitcase">suitcases</a>" known as <i>Bag2Go</i> for air travellers, in conjunction with luggage-maker <a href="/wiki/Rimowa" title="Rimowa">Rimowa</a> and IT firm <a href="/wiki/T-Systems" title="T-Systems">T-Systems</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> The cases feature a collection of built-in electronic gadgets which communicate with a <a href="/wiki/Smartphone_app" class="mw-redirect" title="Smartphone app">smartphone app</a> and with the IT systems of the airline, to assist the traveller and improve reliability and security of <a href="/wiki/Baggage_handling" class="mw-redirect" title="Baggage handling">baggage handling</a>. Gadgets include a <a href="/wiki/Weighing_scale" title="Weighing scale">weighing scale</a> and a location tracker, using <a href="/wiki/GPS" class="mw-redirect" title="GPS">GPS</a> for location tracking, <a href="/wiki/RFID" class="mw-redirect" title="RFID">RFID</a> for identification, and a <a href="/wiki/SIM_card" title="SIM card">SIM card</a> for messaging.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> Since then, similar products have been announced by other companies.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In the late 1990s, Airbus became increasingly interested in developing and selling to the military aviation market. It embarked on two main fields of development: <a href="/wiki/Aerial_refuelling" class="mw-redirect" title="Aerial refuelling">aerial refuelling</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A310_MRTT" title="Airbus A310 MRTT">Airbus A310 MRTT</a> (Multi-Role Tanker Transport) and the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A330_MRTT" title="Airbus A330 MRTT">Airbus A330 MRTT</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tactical_airlift" class="mw-redirect" title="Tactical airlift">tactical airlift</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A400M_Atlas" title="Airbus A400M Atlas">Airbus A400M Atlas</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Airbus_A400M_Rollout.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Airbus_A400M_Rollout.JPG/220px-Airbus_A400M_Rollout.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Airbus_A400M_Rollout.JPG/330px-Airbus_A400M_Rollout.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Airbus_A400M_Rollout.JPG/440px-Airbus_A400M_Rollout.JPG 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Airbus_A400M_Rollout.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The first <a href="/wiki/A400M" class="mw-redirect" title="A400M">A400M</a> in Seville, 26 June 2008</div></div></div>\n<p>In January 1999 Airbus established a separate company, Airbus Military <small>SAS</small>, to undertake development and production of a turboprop-powered <a href="/wiki/Airlift" title="Airlift">tactical transport</a> aircraft, the A400M.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> The A400M is being developed by several <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> members, Belgium, France, Germany, <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg" title="Luxembourg">Luxembourg</a>, Spain, Turkey, and the UK, as an alternative to relying on foreign aircraft for <a href="/wiki/Tactical_airlift" class="mw-redirect" title="Tactical airlift">tactical airlift</a> capacity, such as the Ukrainian <a href="/wiki/Antonov_An-124_Ruslan" title="Antonov An-124 Ruslan">Antonov An-124 Ruslan</a><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> and the American <a href="/wiki/C-130_Hercules" class="mw-redirect" title="C-130 Hercules">C-130 Hercules</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> The A400M project has suffered several delays;<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Airbus has threatened to cancel the development unless it receives state subsidies.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FTscrap_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FTscrap-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a> placed an order for the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A310_MRTT" title="Airbus A310 MRTT">Airbus A310 MRTT</a> in 2008, which will be a conversion of an existing airframe as the base model A310 is no longer in production.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> On 25 February 2008 Airbus won an order for three air refuelling MRTT aircraft, adapted from A330 passenger jets, from the United Arab Emirates.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> On 1 March 2008 a consortium of Airbus and <a href="/wiki/Northrop_Grumman" title="Northrop Grumman">Northrop Grumman</a> had won a $35&#160;billion contract to build the new in-flight refuelling aircraft <a href="/wiki/Northrop_Grumman_KC-45" class="mw-redirect" title="Northrop Grumman KC-45">KC-45A</a>, a US built version of the MRTT, for the USAF.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> The decision drew a formal complaint from Boeing,<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/KC-X" title="KC-X">KC-X</a> contract was cancelled to begin bidding afresh.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Airbus_aircraft_numbering_system">Airbus aircraft numbering system</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Airbus aircraft numbering system">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The Airbus numbering system is an alpha numeric model number followed by a dash and a three digit number.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The model number often takes the form of the letter "A" followed by a \'3\', a digit, then followed normally by a \'0\', for example A350. There are some exceptions such as: A220, A318, A319, A321 and A400M. The succeeding three digit number represents the aircraft series, the engine manufacturer and engine version number respectively. To use an A380-800 with Engine Alliance (EA) GP7200 engines as an example; The code is 8 for series 800, 6 for Engine Alliance and engine version 1, thus the aircraft number is A380-861.\n</p><p>An additional letter is sometimes used. These include, \'C\' for a combi version (passenger/freighter), \'F\' for a freighter model, \'R\' for the long range model, and \'X\' for the enhanced model.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Engine_codes">Engine codes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2018:<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"/><div rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#79E491; color:black;">&#160;</span>&#160;Helicopters (9%)</div>\n</div>\n</div></div>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Commercial_aircraft">Commercial aircraft</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Commercial aircraft">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Airbus_A330neo_and_A350_Qatar_Airways.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Airbus_A330neo_and_A350_Qatar_Airways.jpg/220px-Airbus_A330neo_and_A350_Qatar_Airways.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Airbus_A330neo_and_A350_Qatar_Airways.jpg/330px-Airbus_A330neo_and_A350_Qatar_Airways.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Airbus_A330neo_and_A350_Qatar_Airways.jpg/440px-Airbus_A330neo_and_A350_Qatar_Airways.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4227" data-file-height="2818" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Airbus_A330neo_and_A350_Qatar_Airways.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A330neo" title="Airbus A330neo">Airbus A330neo</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Qatar_Airways" title="Qatar Airways">Qatar Airways</a> <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A350-900" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A350-900">Airbus A350-900</a> at <a href="/wiki/Toulouse-Blagnac_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Toulouse-Blagnac Airport">Toulouse-Blagnac Airport</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Commercial aircraft generated 66% of total revenue for the group in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> The product portfolio of such aircraft encompasses short range models such as the A320 family and the world\'s largest passenger airliner, the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A380" title="Airbus A380">A380</a>.\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/EADS_Sogerma" class="mw-redirect" title="EADS Sogerma">EADS Sogerma</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Airbus_Executive_and_Private_Aviation" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus Executive and Private Aviation">Airbus Executive and Private Aviation</a></li></ul>\n<p><b>Airbus Transport International</b>\n</p><p>Airbus Transport International is a cargo airline that operates a fleet of five <a href="/wiki/Airbus_Beluga" title="Airbus Beluga">Airbus Beluga</a> aircraft. The belugas carry aircraft parts from factories to final assembly lines. In 2020, three <a href="/wiki/Airbus_Beluga_XL" title="Airbus Beluga XL">Airbus Beluga XL</a> aircraft which can carry two <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A350_XWB" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A350 XWB">A350</a> wings rather than one Airbus A350 wing. These will slowly replace the five original belugas in the coming years.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Defence_and_space">Defence and space</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Defence and space">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The division <a href="/wiki/Airbus_Defence_and_Space" title="Airbus Defence and Space">Airbus Defence and Space</a> was formed in January 2014 as part of the group restructuring from the former EADS divisions <a href="/wiki/Airbus_Military" title="Airbus Military">Airbus Military</a>, <a href="/wiki/Astrium" title="Astrium">Astrium</a>, and Cassidian (composed of Cassidian Electronics \xe2\x80\x93 develops and manufactures sensors, radars, avionics and electronic warfare systems for military and security applications, Cassidian Air Systems \xe2\x80\x93 develops manned and unmanned aerial systems (UAVs), mission avionics, electronic defence and warning systems and Cassidian Systems \xe2\x80\x93 provides global security systems such as command &amp; control, lead system integration, <a href="/wiki/Terrestrial_Trunked_Radio" title="Terrestrial Trunked Radio">TETRA</a> and <a href="/wiki/TETRAPOL" title="TETRAPOL">TETRAPOL</a> communication systems for public safety, industry, transportation and defence. This line of business was the first one in the world to begin field tests with TETRA Enhanced Data Service (TEDS).<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>).<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/EADS_3_Sigma" title="EADS 3 Sigma">EADS 3 Sigma</a>&#160;&#8211;&#32;a Hellenic company focused in the design, development, production and services provision of airborne and surface target drone systems.</li></ul>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Airbus_Military" title="Airbus Military">Airbus Military</a> division, which manufactured tanker, transport and mission aircraft; <a href="/wiki/Eurocopter" class="mw-redirect" title="Eurocopter">Eurocopter</a>, the world\'s largest helicopter supplier; <a href="/wiki/Astrium" title="Astrium">Astrium</a>, provided systems for aerial, land, naval and civilian security applications including <a href="/wiki/Ariane_(rocket_family)" title="Ariane (rocket family)">Ariane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Galileo_(satellite_navigation)" title="Galileo (satellite navigation)">Galileo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cassidian" class="mw-redirect" title="Cassidian">Cassidian</a>. Through Cassidian, EADS was a partner in the <a href="/wiki/Eurofighter" class="mw-redirect" title="Eurofighter">Eurofighter</a> consortium as well as in the missile systems provider <a href="/wiki/MBDA" title="MBDA">MBDA</a>.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Helicopters">Helicopters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Helicopters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Airbus_Helicopters" title="Airbus Helicopters">Airbus Helicopters</a>, formerly known as Eurocopter, is a helicopter manufacturing and support company. See also: <a href="/wiki/Airbus_Helicopters,_Inc." title="Airbus Helicopters, Inc.">Airbus Helicopters, Inc.</a>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Subsidiaries">Subsidiaries</span><span (previously <i>EADS North America</i>) the U.S. holding company for the North American activities of Airbus Group</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Airbus_Transport_International" class="mw-redirect" K.K. (\xe3\x82\xa8\xe3\x82\xa2\xe3\x83\x90\xe3\x82\xb9\xe3\x83\xbb\xe3\x82\xb8\xe3\x83\xa3\xe3\x83\x91\xe3\x83\xb3\xe6\xa0\xaa\xe5\xbc\x8f\xe4\xbc\x9a\xe7\xa4\xbe) is headquartered in the <a href="/wiki/Roppongi_Hills_Mori_Tower" title="Roppongi Hills Mori Tower">Roppongi Hills Mori Tower</a> in <a href="/wiki/Roppongi" title="Roppongi">Roppongi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minato,_Tokyo" title="Minato, Tokyo">Minato, Tokyo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_manufacturing_presence">International manufacturing presence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: International manufacturing presence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:957px"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto"><a href="/wiki/File:Airbus_Toulouse_plant_entrance_DSC02696.jpg" class="image" title="The main Airbus factory in Blagnac is located next to Toulouse-Blagnac Airport. type=&quot;video/webm; codecs=&amp;quot;vp9, opus&amp;quot;&quot; data-title=&quot;VP9 (360P)&quot; data-shorttitle=&quot;VP9 360P&quot; data-transcodekey=&quot;360p.vp9.webm&quot; data-width=&quot;640&quot; data-height=&quot;360&quot; data-bandwidth=&quot;364616&quot; data-framerate=&quot;25&quot;/&gt;&lt;source src=&quot;//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/5/5c/Welsh_Government_video_-_Airbus_Case_Study%2C_2016.webm/Welsh_Government_video_-_Airbus_Case_Study%2C_2016.webm.360p.webm&quot; type=&quot;video/webm; codecs=&amp;quot;vp8, vorbis&amp;quot;&quot; data-title=&quot;WebM (360P)&quot; data-shorttitle=&quot;WebM 360P&quot; data-transcodekey=&quot;360p.webm&quot; data-width=&quot;640&quot; data-height=&quot;360&quot; data-bandwidth=&quot;580224&quot; data-framerate=&quot;25&quot;/&gt;&lt;/video&gt;&lt;/div&gt;"><img alt="File:Welsh Government video - Airbus Case Study, 2016.webm" style="width:220px;height:124px" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Welsh_Government_video_-_Airbus_Case_Study%2C_2016.webm/220px--Welsh_Government_video_-_Airbus_Case_Study%2C_2016.webm.jpg" /><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/5c/Welsh_Government_video_-_Airbus_Case_Study%2C_2016.webm" title="Play media" target="new"><span class="play-btn-large"><span class="mw-tmh-playtext">Play media</span></span></a></div>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Welsh_Government_video_-_Airbus_Case_Study,_2016.webm" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Airbus factory at <a href="/wiki/Broughton,_Flintshire" title="Broughton, Flintshire">Broughton, Flintshire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">Wales</a>, UK</div></div></div>\n<p>Airbus has several final assembly lines for different models and markets. These are:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Toulouse" title="Toulouse">Toulouse</a>, France (A320, A330 family, A350 family and A380)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hamburg" title="Hamburg">Hamburg</a>, Germany (A318, A319, A320 and A321)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Seville" title="Seville">Seville</a>, Spain (A400M)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Tianjin" title="Tianjin">Tianjin</a>, China (A319 and A320).</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Mobile,_Alabama" title="Mobile, Alabama">Mobile, Alabama</a>, USA \xe2\x80\x94 <a href="/wiki/Airbus_Mobile" title="Airbus Mobile">Airbus Mobile</a> (A220, A319, A320 and A321)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Mirabel" class="mw-redirect" title="Mirabel">Mirabel</a>, Canada (A220)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Broughton,_Flintshire" title="Broughton, Flintshire">Broughton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">Wales</a> \xe2\x80\x94 wings construction<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<p>Airbus, however, has a number of other plants in different European locations, reflecting its foundation as a consortium. An original solution to the problem of moving aircraft parts between the different factories and the assembly plants is the use of the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_Beluga" title="Airbus Beluga">Airbus Beluga</a>, a modified cargo aircraft capable of carrying entire sections of fuselage. Boeing adopted a similar solution with 4 <a href="/wiki/Boeing_Dreamlifter" title="Boeing Dreamlifter">adapted 747-400s</a> to transport the components of the 787. An exception to this scheme is the A380, whose fuselage and wings are too large for sections to be carried by the Beluga. Large A380 parts are brought by ship to <a href="/wiki/Bordeaux" title="Bordeaux">Bordeaux</a>, and then transported to the Toulouse assembly plant by the <a href="/wiki/Itin%C3%A9raire_%C3%A0_Grand_Gabarit" title="Itin\xc3\xa9raire \xc3\xa0 Grand Gabarit">Itin\xc3\xa9raire \xc3\xa0 Grand Gabarit</a>, a specially enlarged waterway and road route.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Airbus opened an assembly plant in <a href="/wiki/Tianjin" title="Tianjin">Tianjin</a>, People\'s Republic of China for its A320 series airliners in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-eads_20061026_pr_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eads_20061026_pr-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> Airbus started constructing a $350&#160;million component manufacturing plant in <a href="/wiki/Harbin" title="Harbin">Harbin</a>, China in July 2009, which will employ 1,000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> Scheduled to be operated by the end of 2010, the 30,000 square metre plant will manufacture composite parts and assemble composite work-packages for the A350 XWB, A320 families and future Airbus programmes. Harbin Aircraft Industry Group Corporation, Hafei Aviation Industry Company Ltd, AviChina Industry &amp; Technology Company and other Chinese partners hold the 80% stake of the plant while Airbus control the remaining 20%.<sup id="cite_ref-China_Daily_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-China_Daily-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>North America is an important region to Airbus in terms of both aircraft sales and suppliers. 2,000 of the total of approximately 5,300 Airbus jetliners sold by Airbus around the world, representing every aircraft in its product line from the 107-seat A318 to the 565-passenger A380, are ordered by North American customers. According to Airbus, US contractors, supporting an estimated 120,000 jobs, earned an estimated $5.5&#160;billion (2003) worth of business. For example, one version of the A380 has 51% American content in terms of work share value. \n</p><p>Plans for a <a href="/wiki/Mobile,_Alabama" title="Mobile, Alabama">Mobile, Alabama</a> aircraft assembly plant were unveiled by Airbus CEO Fabrice Br\xc3\xa9gier from the Mobile Convention Centre on 2 July 2012. The plans include a $600 million factory at the <a href="/wiki/Mobile_Aeroplex_at_Brookley" title="Mobile Aeroplex at Brookley">Mobile Aeroplex at Brookley</a> for the assembly of the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A220" title="Airbus A220">A220</a>, A319, A320 and <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A321" title="Airbus A321">A321</a> aircraft.  It could employ up to 1,000 full-time workers when operational.  Construction began on 8 April 2013, and became operable by 2015,<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> producing up to 50 aircraft per year by 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-apconfirm_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-apconfirm-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bbcconfirm_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcconfirm-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In February 2019, Airbus stated that production of the A380 will end in 2021 after Emirates, the biggest customer for the plane, reduced its outstanding order for 53 planes to just fourteen.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Financial_information">Financial information</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Financial information">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="box-Update plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" class="thumbinner" style="width:202px">\n<div style="background-color:white;margin:auto;position:relative;width:200px;height:200px;overflow:hidden;border-radius:100px;border:1px solid black">\n<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:firebrick"></div><div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;right:100px; top:0; border-width:0 82.727194597248px 100px 0; border-right-color:#290192"></div>\n<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;right:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 100px 0;border-color:#290192"></div>\n</div>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<p>Revenues by region, as of 2013:<sup id="cite_ref-applications.airbus-group.com_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-applications.airbus-group.com-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#290192; color:white;">&#160;</span>&#160;Europe (36%)</div><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="background-color:firebrick; color:white;">&#160;</span>&#160;Asia-Pacific (33%)</div><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="background-color:lightgrey; color:black;">&#160;</span>&#160;North America (15%)</div><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="background-color:gold; color:black;">&#160;</span>&#160;Middle East (9%)</div><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#71B600; color:black;">&#160;</span>&#160;Africa and Latin America (7%)</div>\n</div>\n</div></div>\n<p>In October 2005 the British <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defence_(United_Kingdom)" title="Ministry of Defence (United Kingdom)">Ministry of Defence</a> warned European politicians to stop, as it sees it, interfering in the corporate governance of EADS. The former UK Defence Procurement Minister <a href="/wiki/Paul_Drayson,_Baron_Drayson" title="Paul Drayson, Baron Drayson">Lord Drayson</a> hinted that the UK government, a major customer for EADS, may withhold future contracts. "As a key customer, we see it as important for EADS to move in a direction that is free from political interference."<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 4 April 2006, DaimlerChrysler announced its intention to reduce its shareholding from 30&#8201;% to 22.5&#8201;%. The company places a value of the stake at "approximately \xe2\x82\xac2.0 billion."<sup id="cite_ref-DaimlerReduce_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DaimlerReduce-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> Lagard\xc3\xa8re will reduce its holding by an identical amount. However, <a href="/wiki/Caisse_des_D%C3%A9p%C3%B4ts_et_Consignations" class="mw-redirect" title="Caisse des D\xc3\xa9p\xc3\xb4ts et Consignations">Caisse des D\xc3\xa9p\xc3\xb4ts et Consignations</a>, a unit of the French government, acquired 2.25&#8201;% of EADS. At issue as a result is the fact that the German and French shareholdings are now in imbalance.<sup id="cite_ref-iht_20060411_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iht_20060411-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 30 August 2006, shortly after the stock price decline caused by the A380 delivery delays, more than 5&#8201;% of EADS stock has been reportedly purchased by the Russian state-owned <a href="/wiki/Vneshtorgbank" class="mw-redirect" title="Vneshtorgbank">Vneshtorgbank</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-vneshtorgbank_yahoo_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vneshtorgbank_yahoo-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> Now its share is nearly 6&#8201;%. In December 2007, Vneshtorgbank sold EADS shares to another state-controlled bank <a href="/wiki/Vneshekonombank" class="mw-redirect" title="Vneshekonombank">Vneshekonombank</a>. EADS sharers are to be delivered by <a href="/wiki/Vneshekonombank" class="mw-redirect" title="Vneshekonombank">Vneshekonombank</a> to the charter capital of JSC "<a href="/wiki/United_Aircraft_Corporation" title="United Aircraft Corporation">United Aircraft Corporation</a>" in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 3 October 2006, shortly after EADS admitted further delays in the Airbus 380 programme would cost the company 4.8 billion euros in lost earnings in 2010, EADS shares, traded on the Paris arm of Euronext, were suspended after they surpassed the 10&#8201;% loss limit. Trading resumed later in the day with the one-day loss holding at 7&#8201;%.\n</p><p>In 2007, <a href="/wiki/Dubai_Holding" title="Dubai Holding">Dubai Holding</a> acquired 3.12&#8201;% of EADS stock, making the Dubai buy-out fund one of the largest institutional shareholders.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2008, EADS had arms sales equivalent of $17.9 billion, which constituted 28&#8201;% of total revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-SIPRItable_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SIPRItable-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In April 2013, Daimler sold its shares in EADS.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As of 22&#160;June&#160;2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Airbus&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, 73.6&#8201;% of Airbus Group stock is publicly traded on six European stock exchanges, while the remaining 26.4&#8201;% is owned by a "Contractual Partnership". As at 26 April 2018, the partnership is owned by <a href="/wiki/SOGEPA" title="SOGEPA">SOGEPA</a> (11.1%), GZBV (11.1%) and <a href="/wiki/SEPI" class="mw-redirect" title="SEPI">SEPI</a> (4.2%). SOGEPA is owned by the French State, GZBV is majority owned by <a href="/wiki/KfW" title="KfW">KfW</a>, while SEPI is a Spanish state holding company.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In April 2020, Airbus announced that it has cut aircraft production by a third due to the COVID-19 outbreak. According to Guillaume Faury, the company was "bleeding cash at an unprecedented speed." The recession put its survival at stake and presented the need for deep job cuts throughout all Airbus departments. 3,000 workers in France were involved in government-assisted furlough schemes.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="text-align:right;">\n\n<tbody><tr style="background:#ffdead;">\n<th style="width:250px;">Finances<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>\n</th>\n<th style="width:40px;">2013\n</th>\n<th style="width:40px;">2012\n</th>\n<th style="width:40px;">2011\n</th>\n<th style="width:40px;">2010\n</th>\n<th style="width:40px;">2009\n</th>\n<th style="width:40px;">2008\n</th>\n<th style="width:40px;">2007\n</th>\n<th style="width:40px;">2006\n</th>\n<th style="width:40px;">2005\n</th>\n<th style="width:40px;">2004\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="text-align:left">Sales EUR billion\n</th>\n<td>59.256\n</td>\n<td>56.480\n</td>\n<td>49.128\n</td>\n<td>45.752\n</td>\n<td>42.822\n</td>\n<td>43.265\n</td>\n<td>39.123\n</td>\n<td>39.434\n</td>\n<td>34.206\n</td>\n<td>31.761\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="text-align:left">EBITDA in Mio. style="text-align:left">Order backlog at 31.12. in EUR million\n</th>\n<td>686.734\n</td>\n<td>566.463\n</td>\n<td>540.978\n</td>\n<td>448.493\n</td>\n<td>389.067\n</td>\n<td>400.248\n</td>\n<td>339.532\n</td>\n<td>262.810\n</td>\n<td>253.235\n</td>\n<td>184.288\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="text-align:left">Employees (number) 31.12.\n</th>\n<td>144.061\n</td>\n<td>140.405\n</td>\n<td>133.115\n</td>\n<td>121.691\n</td>\n<td>119.506\n</td>\n<td>118.349\n</td>\n<td>116.493\n</td>\n<td>116.805\n</td>\n<td>113.210\n</td>\n<td>110.662\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:left" colspan="11"><small>accounted for under IFRS; The fiscal year ends on 31/12.</small>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Sales of military equipment in 2012 amounted to 15.4 billion US dollars.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_record">Environmental record</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Environmental record">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Airbus has committed to the "Flightpath 2050", an aviation industry plan to reduce noise, CO<sub>2</sub>, and <a href="/wiki/NOx" title="NOx">NOx</a> emissions.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Airbus was the first aerospace business to become ISO 14001 certified, in January 2007; this is a broader certification covering the whole organisation, not just the aircraft it produces.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In association with <a href="/wiki/Honeywell" title="Honeywell">Honeywell</a> and <a href="/wiki/JetBlue" title="JetBlue">JetBlue</a> Airbus has developed a <a href="/wiki/Biofuel" title="Biofuel">biofuel</a> to reduce pollution and dependence on fossil fuels, claiming that this has the potential to replace up to a third of the world\'s aviation fuel. Algae-based biofuel absorbs carbon dioxide during growth and does not compete with food production. This alternative may be commercially available by 2030 but algae and other vegetation-based fuels are in an early stage of development and fuel-bearing algae has been expensive to develop.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> Airbus offers delivery flights to airlines using a 10% biofuel blend in standard engines. The fuel does not cut carbon emissions but is free of sulphur emissions and demonstrates that the fuel could be used in commercial flights in unmodified engines.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In September 2020, Airbus unveiled three <a href="/wiki/Liquid_hydrogen" title="Liquid hydrogen">liquid hydrogen</a>-fueled "ZEROe" concept aircraft that it claims could become the first commercial zero-emission aircraft, entering service by 2035.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversies">Controversies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Controversies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_subsidies">Government subsidies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Government subsidies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Boeing has continually protested over "launch aid" and other forms of government aid to Airbus, while Airbus has argued that Boeing receives illegal subsidies through military and research contracts and tax breaks.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In July 2004 former Boeing CEO <a href="/wiki/Harry_Stonecipher" title="Harry Stonecipher">Harry Stonecipher</a> accused Airbus of abusing a 1992 bilateral EU-US agreement providing for disciplines for large civil aircraft support from governments. Airbus is given reimbursable launch investment (RLI), called "launch aid" by the US, from European governments with the money being paid back with interest plus indefinite royalties, but only if the aircraft is a commercial success.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> Airbus contends that this system is fully compliant with the 1992 agreement and <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">WTO</a> rules. The agreement allows up to 33% of the programme cost to be met through government loans which are to be fully repaid within 17 years with interest and royalties. These loans are held at a minimum interest rate equal to the cost of government borrowing plus 0.25%, which would be below market rates available to Airbus without government support.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated4_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated4-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> Airbus claims that since the signature of the EU-US agreement in 1992, it has repaid European governments more than U.S.$6.7&#160;billion and that this is 40% more than it has received.\n</p><p>Airbus argues that the military contracts awarded to Boeing, the second largest U.S. defence contractor, are in effect a form of subsidy, such as the controversy surrounding the Boeing <a href="/wiki/KC-767" class="mw-redirect" title="KC-767">KC-767</a> military contracting arrangements. The significant U.S. government support of technology development via <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> also provides significant support to Boeing, as do the large tax breaks offered to Boeing, which some people claim are in violation of the 1992 agreement and <a href="/wiki/WTO" class="mw-redirect" title="WTO">WTO</a> rules. In its recent products such as the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_787_Dreamliner" title="Boeing 787 Dreamliner">787</a>, Boeing has also been offered direct financial support from local and state governments.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In January 2005 the European Union and United States trade representatives, <a href="/wiki/Peter_Mandelson" title="Peter Mandelson">Peter Mandelson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Robert_Zoellick" title="Robert Zoellick">Robert Zoellick</a> respectively, agreed to talks aimed at resolving the increasing tensions.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> These talks were not successful with the dispute becoming more acrimonious rather than approaching a settlement.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>WTO ruled in August 2010 and in May 2011 that Airbus had received improper government subsidies through loans with below market rates from several European countries.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> In a separate ruling in February 2011, WTO found that Boeing had received local and federal aid in violation of WTO rules.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cluster_bomb_allegation">Cluster bomb allegation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Cluster bomb allegation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 2005 the <a href="/wiki/Government_Pension_Fund_of_Norway" title="Government Pension Fund of Norway">Government Pension Fund of Norway</a> recommended the exclusion of several companies producing <a href="/wiki/Cluster_bomb" class="mw-redirect" title="Cluster bomb">cluster bombs</a> or components. EADS and its sister company EADS Finance BV were among them, arguing that EADS manufactures "key components for cluster bombs". The criticism was centred around TDA, a joint venture between EADS and Thales&#160;S.A. TDA produced the <a href="/wiki/Mortar_(weapon)" title="Mortar (weapon)">mortar</a> ammunition PR&#160;Cargo, which can be considered cluster ammunition, however this definition has since been successfully battled by EADS. EADS and its subsidiaries are now regarded as fulfilling all the conditions of the <a href="/wiki/Ottawa_Treaty" title="Ottawa Treaty">Ottawa Treaty</a>. According to the new point of view, no product of EADS or its <a href="/wiki/Subsidiaries" class="mw-redirect" title="Subsidiaries">subsidiaries</a> falls into the category of <a href="/wiki/Antipersonnel_mine" class="mw-redirect" title="Antipersonnel mine">antipersonnel mines</a> as defined by the Ottawa Treaty ("<a href="/wiki/Landmine" class="mw-redirect" title="Landmine">landmines</a> under the Ottawa Treaty"). In April 2006, the fund declared that the basis for excluding EADS from investments related to production of <a href="/wiki/Cluster_munition" title="Cluster munition">cluster munitions</a> is no longer valid, however its shareholding of MBDA means the fund still excludes EADS due to its indirect involvement in <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapon" title="Nuclear weapon">nuclear weapons</a> production.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Insider_trading_investigation">Insider trading investigation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Insider trading investigation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 2 June 2006 co-CEO No\xc3\xabl Forgeard and Airbus CEO <a href="/wiki/Gustav_Humbert" title="Gustav Humbert">Gustav Humbert</a> resigned following the controversy caused by the June 2006 announcement that deliveries of the A380 would be delayed by a further six months. Forgeard was one of a number of executives including <a href="/wiki/Jean-Paul_Gut" title="Jean-Paul Gut">Jean-Paul Gut</a> who exercised <a href="/wiki/Stock_option" class="mw-redirect" title="Stock option">stock options</a> in November 2005 and March 2006. He and twenty-one other executives are<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (March 2019)">when?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> under investigation as to whether they knew about the delays in the Airbus&#160;A380 project which caused a 26&#8201;% fall in EADS shares when publicised.\nThe French government\'s actions were also under investigation; The state-owned bank Caisse des D\xc3\xa9pots et Consignations (CDC) bought part of Lagard\xc3\xa8re\'s 7.5&#8201;% stake in EADS in April 2006, allowing that latter to partially escape the June 2006 losses.<sup id="cite_ref-economist11oct2007_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-economist11oct2007-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bribery_allegations">Bribery allegations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Bribery allegations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Africa">South Africa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: South Africa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>In 2003 <a href="/wiki/Tony_Yengeni" title="Tony Yengeni">Tony Yengeni</a>, former <a href="/wiki/Chief_whip" class="mw-redirect" title="Chief whip">chief whip</a> of South Africa\'s <a href="/wiki/African_National_Congress" title="African National Congress">African National Congress</a>, was convicted of fraud worth around US$5&#160;billion relating to an arms deal with South Africa, in which Airbus (formerly EADS) were major players,.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> It was claimed that Airbus had admitted that it had "rendered assistance" to around thirty senior officials, including defence force chief General <a href="/wiki/Siphiwe_Nyanda" title="Siphiwe Nyanda">Siphiwe Nyanda</a>, to obtain luxury vehicles.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> In March 2003,  South Africa withdrew all charges of bribery against the former head of EADS South Africa,<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> and in September 2004, the prosecutor\'s office dismissed the bribery charges against Yengeni.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Saudi_Arabia">Saudi Arabia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Saudi Arabia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>In August 2012 the UK\'s <a href="/wiki/Serious_Fraud_Office_(United_Kingdom)" title="Serious Fraud Office (United Kingdom)">Serious Fraud Office</a> opened a criminal investigation into an EADS subsidiary, GPT Special Project Management&#160;Ltd, regarding bribery allegations made by GPT\'s former programme director, Ian Foxley. Foxley alleged that luxury cars were bought for senior Saudis, and that millions of <a href="/wiki/Pound_sterling" title="Pound sterling">pounds sterling</a> were paid to mysterious <a href="/wiki/Cayman_Islands" title="Cayman Islands">Cayman Islands</a> companies, possibly to secure a \xc2\xa32&#160;billion contract to renew the <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabian_National_Guard" title="Saudi Arabian National Guard">Saudi Arabian National Guard</a>\'s military telecommunications network.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> Foxley\'s allegations were supported by two other GPT employees.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> The later agreement between Airbus and the SFO on 31 January 2020 excluded settlement of this case.<sup id="cite_ref-SFO2mar2020_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SFO2mar2020-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="British_and_French_investigations">British and French investigations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: British and French investigations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Parquet_national_financier" title="Parquet national financier">French National Financial Prosecutor\'s Office</a> (PNF), the UK <a href="/wiki/Serious_Fraud_Office_(United_Kingdom)" title="Serious Fraud Office (United Kingdom)">Serious Fraud Office</a> (SFO) and the US Department of Justice (DoJ) had been jointly investigating irregularities in Airbus marketing practices since 2016, in particular the activities of agents Saudi Arabia, Kazakhstan, the Philippines, Indonesia and Austria,<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;a&#93;</a></sup> but also China, the United Arab Emirates, South Korea, Japan, Saudi Arabia, Taiwan, Kuwait, Turkey, Russia, Mexico, Brazil, Vietnam, India, Colombia and Nepal.<sup id="cite_ref-SFO2mar2020_125-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SFO2mar2020-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In July 2016, SFO opened a criminal investigation into "suspicions of fraud, bribes and corruption" after Airbus informed British authorities of a failure to disclose the role played by some intermediaries facilitating the sale of aircraft. Airbus was required to provide this information in order to benefit from export credits, which the British, French and German governments had suspended. In March 2017, the PNF subsequently opened a preliminary investigation into "suspicions of fraud and corruption in civil aviation activities" in cooperation with the SFO.<sup id="cite_ref-SFO2mar2020_125-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SFO2mar2020-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The allegations included that from 2012 onwards Airbus was responsible for recruiting and remunerating intermediaries to influence the award of civil and military contracts. Payments worth hundreds of millions of euros in alleged secret commissions were made and numerous sales including in Saudi Arabia, Kazakhstan, Philippines, Indonesia, Austria, China and Mauritius were under suspicion of bribery.<sup id="cite_ref-mediapart1aug2017_126-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mediapart1aug2017-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag needs to be fact-checked with the cited source(s). (May 2020)">verification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup id="cite_ref-FT31jan2020_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FT31jan2020-128">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The investigation focussed on the Airbus, Strategy and Marketing Organization (SMO), the department responsible for negotiating sales contracts and which, La Tribune reported as having "a network and an incredible influence around the world." Directed successively by <a href="/wiki/Jean-Paul_Gut" title="Jean-Paul Gut">Jean-Paul Gut</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marwan_Lahoud" title="Marwan Lahoud">Marwan Lahoud</a>, the SMO was dissolved in 2016 under the new executive director, Thomas Enders, as part of a \xe2\x80\x9cclean hands\xe2\x80\x9d operation.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2014, in a case referred to as the Kazakhgate affair, a search at <a href="/wiki/Airbus_Helicopters" title="Airbus Helicopters">Airbus Helicopters</a> by French authorities found emails confirming that Airbus had agreed in principle to pay \xe2\x82\xac12 million in pots of wine to the Prime Minister of Kazakhstan to facilitate the sale of helicopters. Officers from the Central Anti-Corruption Office (OCLCIFF) then searched the home of <a href="/wiki/Marwan_Lahoud" title="Marwan Lahoud">Marwan Lahoud</a> on 8 February 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;b&#93;</a></sup> This revealed that two Turkish intermediaries had claimed payment of commissions due in connection with the sale of 160 aircraft to China valued at US$10 billion. A message by Lahoud suggested that the commissions could reach US$250 million. The SMO was to conceal these commissions as false invoices for a fictitious Caspian pipeline project.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;c&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In January 2020, French, British and American courts validated three agreements between Airbus and the PNF,<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> the UK SFO,<sup id="cite_ref-SFO2mar2020_125-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SFO2mar2020-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> and the US DoJ.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> Airbus recognised the charges and agreed to pay fines of \xe2\x82\xac3.6 billion in France, \xe2\x82\xac984 million in the United Kingdom and \xe2\x82\xac526 million in the United States. The penalties were the highest ever issued by the French and British bodies.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>These settlements close the prosecution of Airbus regarding the Kazakhstan case but not allegations of misconduct in Saudi Arabia, China and Turkey, which Airbus denies.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> Airbus managers may still be pursued as private individuals.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;d&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Airbus_Training_Centre_Europe" title="Airbus Training Centre Europe">Airbus Training Centre Europe</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Aerospace_industry_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Aerospace industry in the United Kingdom">Aerospace industry in the United Kingdom</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Airbus_affair" title="Airbus affair">Airbus affair</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Boeing" title="Boeing">Boeing</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Bombardier_Aerospace" class="mw-redirect" title="Bombardier Aerospace">Bombardier Aerospace</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Comac" title="Comac">Comac</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Competition_between_Airbus_and_Boeing" title="Competition between Airbus and Boeing">Competition between Airbus and Boeing</a></li>\n<li><a title="Embraer">Embraer</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Liebherr_Aerospace" title="Liebherr Aerospace">Liebherr Aerospace</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/United_Aircraft_Corporation" title="United Aircraft Corporation">United Aircraft Corporation</a></li></ul>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span
